<p><b>David Benjamin James</b> <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">MBE</a> (born 1 August 1970) is an English former <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who played as a <a href="/wiki/Goalkeeper_(association_football)" title="Goalkeeper (association football)">goalkeeper</a>. He most recently served as the player–manager at <a href="/wiki/Kerala_Blasters_FC" title="Kerala Blasters FC">Kerala Blasters FC</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Super_League" title="Indian Super League">Indian Super League</a>. He is currently a regular pundit on <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a>'s football coverage.</p>
<p>James is fourth on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_players" title="List of Premier League players">list of all-time Premier League appearances</a>, having played in 572 top-level matches, and held the Premier League <a href="/wiki/Football_records_in_England#Goalkeepers" title="Football records in England">record for most clean sheets</a> with 170 until <a href="/wiki/Petr_%C4%8Cech" title="Petr Čech">Petr Čech</a> surpassed this record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was capped 53 times by <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> between 1997 and 2010, and was first choice goalkeeper during the team's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">Euro 2004</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 World Cup</a> campaigns. He was appointed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Member of the Order of the British Empire">Member of the Order of the British Empire</a> (MBE) in the 2012 Birthday Honours for services to football and charity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MBE_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-MBE-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Having started his career with <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>, James went on to feature in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a>. He gained a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">Football League Cup</a> winner's medal with <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_FA_Cup" title="1994–95 FA Cup">1995</a>, an <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> winner's medal with <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> in <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_FA_Cup" title="2007–08 FA Cup">2008</a>, as well as runners-up medals with <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> in <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_FA_Cup" title="1999–2000 FA Cup">2000</a>, Liverpool in <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_FA_Cup" title="1995–96 FA Cup">1996</a> and Portsmouth in <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_FA_Cup" title="2009–10 FA Cup">2010</a>. In 2010, at the age of 39, he became the oldest goalkeeper to appear in an <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">FA Cup Final</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OldestKeeperFACup_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-OldestKeeperFACup-6">[6]</a></sup> James dropped down a division in 2010 to play for <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a> and later played for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_One" title="Football League One">League One</a> side <a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a>. He joined Icelandic side <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%8DBV_Vestmannaeyjar" title="ÍBV Vestmannaeyjar">ÍBV Vestmannaeyjar</a> in 2013 in a joint playing and coaching capacity, before officially retiring.</p>
<p>In October 2013, James took up a coaching position at <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a>, the club he has supported since his childhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The following year, he became the marquee player and manager of the newly formed Kerala Blasters.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Watford">Watford</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Watford">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Welwyn_Garden_City" title="Welwyn Garden City">Welwyn Garden City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a>, James grew up supporting <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> He signed as a trainee with Luton's <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C.%E2%80%93Watford_F.C._rivalry" title="Luton Town F.C.–Watford F.C. rivalry">local rivals</a> <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> upon leaving school, and was first selected for the club's senior team in 1989. In his days as a youth player, he helped Watford win the <a href="/wiki/FA_Youth_Cup" title="FA Youth Cup">FA Youth Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globeandmail_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-globeandmail-10">[10]</a></sup> Following the departure of <a href="/wiki/Tony_Coton" title="Tony Coton">Tony Coton</a>, James made his league debut on 25 August 1990 in a 1–2 defeat against <a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall</a>, and his performance resulted in an <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">England U21</a> call-up for a match against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_under-21_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland under-21 national football team">Republic of Ireland</a>. He earned a total of ten caps for the U21s.</p>
<p>At club level, James made 89 first-team appearances for Watford, and was named the club's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Watford_F.C._Players_of_the_Season" title="List of Watford F.C. Players of the Season">Player of the Season</a> for the <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_in_English_football" title="1990–91 in English football">1990–91 season</a>, when he kept goal in all 46 <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a> games as Watford escaped relegation. He was signed for £1.25m by <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> on 6 July 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In 2008, James was inducted into the Watford Hall of Fame for his services to the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liverpool">Liverpool</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Liverpool">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>James made his Liverpool debut on 16 August 1992 in a 0–1 league defeat to <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> After conceding twenty goals in eleven matches in the first half of the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_in_English_football" title="1993–94 in English football">1993–94</a>, he was dropped in favour of veteran <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Grobbelaar" title="Bruce Grobbelaar">Bruce Grobbelaar</a>, but was recalled to the starting line-up and kept his first clean sheet of the season in a 1–0 away win over <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> on 31 January 1993, which included a penalty save from <a href="/wiki/Paul_Merson" title="Paul Merson">Paul Merson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> He also received a runners-up medal in <a href="/wiki/1996_FA_Cup_Final" title="1996 FA Cup Final">1996</a> in the FA Cup while being on the losing side against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>.</p>
<p>James rose to fame together with Liverpool teammates <a href="/wiki/Steve_McManaman" title="Steve McManaman">Steve McManaman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Redknapp" title="Jamie Redknapp">Jamie Redknapp</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a>, who were nicknamed the "<a href="/wiki/Spice_Boys_(footballers)" title="Spice Boys (footballers)">Spice Boys</a>" – an epithet named after the <a href="/wiki/Spice_Girls" title="Spice Girls">Spice Girls</a> that was used by those who alleged the Liverpool team of the 1990s were more focused on partying than winning games. James' frequent blunders earned him the nickname <i><a href="/wiki/Calamity_James" title="Calamity James">Calamity James</a></i>. He put down his spate of errors to an overindulgence in playing computer games that in turn affected his concentration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-15">[15]</a></sup> Despite winning the 1995 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" title="Football League Cup">Football League Cup</a>, James' hold on the starting position was put in jeopardy with the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Brad_Friedel" title="Brad Friedel">Brad Friedel</a>. On 23 June 1999, after 277 games for Liverpool, he was sold to <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> for £1.8m.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aston_Villa">Aston Villa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Aston Villa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>James made his Villa debut on 7 August 1999, and kept a clean sheet in a 1–0 away win over <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> in the opening <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> game. He was decisive in a penalty <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout_(football)" title="Penalty shootout (football)">shoot-out</a> against <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> in the 2000 <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> semi-final, but was at fault for <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>'s winning goal in the ensuing final, the last to be staged at the <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">old Wembley</a>.</p>
<p>After just two years and 85 appearances, James moved to <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> for £3.5 million on 11 July 2001, signing a four-year contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thisislondon_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-thisislondon-17">[17]</a></sup> However, a serious knee injury sustained while on international duty kept him out for several months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-knee_injury_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-knee_injury-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Ham_United">West Ham United</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: West Ham United">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>James made his debut for <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham</a> on 24 November 2001 in a 1–0 home loss to <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Premier_League" title="2002–03 Premier League">2002–03</a>, West Ham were relegated to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a>. James stayed with West Ham at the start of the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Football_League_First_Division" title="2003–04 Football League First Division">2003–04 season</a> before returning to the Premier League, signing for <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> on 14 January 2004 for an undisclosed fee as a replacement for the retired <a href="/wiki/David_Seaman" title="David Seaman">David Seaman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-undisclosed_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-undisclosed-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> He played 102 total games in all competitions for West Ham.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_City">Manchester City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Manchester City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>James made his <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> debut on 17 January 2004 in a 1–1 home draw with <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> City won only four of the seventeen matches that James started, two of which came after James saved penalties against <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> James said that exploring the field of <a href="/wiki/Sport_psychology" title="Sport psychology">sport psychology</a> improved his skills as a goalkeeper, particularly saving penalty kicks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the last day of the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_FA_Premier_League" title="2004–05 FA Premier League">2004–05 season</a>, James was playing for City who needed to beat <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_UEFA_Cup" title="2005–06 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>. With five minutes remaining the score was 1–1, when City's manager <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Pearce" title="Stuart Pearce">Stuart Pearce</a> substituted midfielder <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Reyna" title="Claudio Reyna">Claudio Reyna</a> for the substitute goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Nicky_Weaver" title="Nicky Weaver">Nicky Weaver</a>, and James was moved to play in attack for the remainder of the game. The unusual tactic almost worked when, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Injury_time" title="Injury time">injury time</a>, Middlesbrough defender <a href="/wiki/Franck_Queudrue" title="Franck Queudrue">Franck Queudrue</a> conceded a penalty by handling a cross that was aimed at James. However, <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a>'s penalty was saved by Middlesbrough goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Mark_Schwarzer" title="Mark Schwarzer">Mark Schwarzer</a> and so Middlesbrough not City qualified for the UEFA Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 August 2006, James, who had separated from his wife, stated that he needed to leave Manchester City to be closer to his children, who lived in London. Manchester City confirmed they had accepted a bid from <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pompey_bid_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-pompey_bid-27">[27]</a></sup> Two days later, he joined Portsmouth for £1.2 million, signing a two-year deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pompey_move_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-pompey_move-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portsmouth">Portsmouth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Portsmouth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_James_warmup_2010_FA_Cup_Final_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3312" data-file-width="4416" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/David_James_warmup_2010_FA_Cup_Final_2.jpg/170px-David_James_warmup_2010_FA_Cup_Final_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/David_James_warmup_2010_FA_Cup_Final_2.jpg/255px-David_James_warmup_2010_FA_Cup_Final_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/David_James_warmup_2010_FA_Cup_Final_2.jpg/340px-David_James_warmup_2010_FA_Cup_Final_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:David_James_warmup_2010_FA_Cup_Final_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
James during his time at Portsmouth.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>James kept clean sheets in his first five appearances for Portsmouth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> On 22 April 2007, James kept his 142nd <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" title="FA Premier League">Premier League</a> clean sheet in a goalless draw with Aston Villa, breaking the record of 141 previously held by <a href="/wiki/David_Seaman" title="David Seaman">David Seaman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> At the end of <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Portsmouth_F.C._season" title="2006–07 Portsmouth F.C. season">2006–07</a>, James was named Portsmouth's <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C.#Portsmouth_Player_of_the_Season_.28since_1968.29" title="Portsmouth F.C.">player of the season</a>.</p>
<p>James has made the most league appearances<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> of any goalkeeper since the formation of the Premier League over fifteen seasons, in addition to conceding the most goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> On 30 January 2008, in a league match against Manchester United, he became the third player (after <a href="/wiki/Gary_Speed" title="Gary Speed">Gary Speed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a>) to cross the 500-match threshold.</p>
<p>James signed a one-year contract extension in May 2007, which kept him at <a href="/wiki/Fratton_Park" title="Fratton Park">Fratton Park</a> until the end of the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Portsmouth_F.C._season" title="2008–09 Portsmouth F.C. season">2008–09 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> James won the second major trophy of his career during that season, as Portsmouth claimed a 1–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2008_FA_Cup_Final" title="2008 FA Cup Final">2008 FA Cup Final</a>. On 8 November 2008, he made his 100th appearance for Portsmouth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>He holds the distinction of twice having been the record holder for consecutive Premier League appearances, with 159 during his Liverpool days from February 1994 to February 1998, and 166 between Manchester City and Portsmouth from 2006 to 2008; both streaks were eventually topped by <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a> and Tottenham Hotspur's <a href="/wiki/Brad_Friedel" title="Brad Friedel">Brad Friedel</a>, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-friedel_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-friedel-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 February 2009 against Manchester City, James made his 536th Premier League appearance, breaking <a href="/wiki/Gary_Speed" title="Gary Speed">Gary Speed</a>'s all-time record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-speed_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-speed-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 April 2009, Times Online named James as the 15th greatest player in Portsmouth's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>James captained Portsmouth in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_FA_Cup" title="2009–10 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> semi-final against Tottenham Hotspur where Portsmouth won 2–0 in extra time, describing the experience as "superb".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-massive_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-massive-38">[38]</a></sup> He also captained the team in <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">the final</a> as Portsmouth were beaten 1–0 by <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Chelsea_F.C._season" title="2009–10 Chelsea F.C. season">double winners</a> <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>.</p>
<p>His contract expired at the end of the 2009–10 season, and he expressed interest in succeeding <a href="/wiki/Avram_Grant" title="Avram Grant">Avram Grant</a> as Portsmouth manager,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> though this came to nothing. The club offered him a new playing contract, but withdrew the offer after he failed to commit to the club; therefore, James left Portsmouth and became a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_Agent" title="Free Agent">free agent</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bristol_City">Bristol City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Bristol City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_James_taking_goal_kick.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1632" data-file-width="2640" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/David_James_taking_goal_kick.jpg/220px-David_James_taking_goal_kick.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/David_James_taking_goal_kick.jpg/330px-David_James_taking_goal_kick.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/David_James_taking_goal_kick.jpg/440px-David_James_taking_goal_kick.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:David_James_taking_goal_kick.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
James playing for <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Severnside_derby" title="Severnside derby">Severnside derby</a> against <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a>, 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>James signed a one-year contract with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" title="Football League Championship">Championship</a> side <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a> on 30 July 2010, with the option of a second year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-news_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-news-41">[41]</a></sup> He stated that he hoped that his performances at the club would keep him on the radar for the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England team</a> and that his decision to join them was motivated by a desire to be closer to his family home in <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>James' league debut for Bristol City came on 7 August 2010 in a 3–0 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> On 11 February 2011, the eve of his 850th club appearance, James announced he had signed a contract extension with the club until June 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> On 10 March 2012, James reached 900 club appearances in a game against <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Severnside_derby" title="Severnside derby">Severnside derby</a>, in which he was made captain as a mark of respect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-900app_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-900app-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was released by Bristol City on 1 May 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> and in July 2012 began training with <a href="/wiki/Exeter_City_F.C." title="Exeter City F.C.">Exeter City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Bournemouth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 27 September 2012, he arrived at <a href="/wiki/Dean_Court" title="Dean Court">Dean Court</a> to train with <a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a>, signing a one-year deal to play for them the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> However he did not see out the contract, leaving the club by mutual consent in March 2013 after making 19 appearances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".C3.8DBV_Vestmannaeyjar">ÍBV Vestmannaeyjar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: ÍBV Vestmannaeyjar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 2 April 2013, James signed a contract with Icelandic club <a href="/wiki/%C3%8D%C3%BEr%C3%B3ttabandalag_Vestmannaeyja" title="Íþróttabandalag Vestmannaeyja">ÍBV</a> until the end of the <a href="/wiki/2013_%C3%9Arvalsdeild" title="2013 Úrvalsdeild">2013 season</a> in a joint player/coach capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> He linked up with former <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> teammate <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Hrei%C3%B0arsson" title="Hermann Hreiðarsson">Hermann Hreiðarsson</a>, the manager of ÍBV. The ÍBV chairman stated that James was not being paid high wages, and that he was primarily playing out of kindness and to gain coaching experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> His arrival at ÍBV saw much higher attendances than in previous years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> ÍBV ended the season in sixth position, and James announced his retirement from playing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kerala_Blasters_FC">Kerala Blasters FC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Kerala Blasters FC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>He was signed by <a href="/wiki/Kerala_Blasters_FC" title="Kerala Blasters FC">Kerala Blasters FC</a>, owned by <a href="/wiki/Sachin_Tendulkar" title="Sachin Tendulkar">Sachin Tendulkar</a>, for the <a href="/wiki/2014_Indian_Super_League_season" title="2014 Indian Super League season">2014 Indian Super League season</a> as a player-manager. He said "I hope my involvement with ISL will be the start of something great."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KB_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-KB-54">[54]</a></sup> The team's first fixture on 13 October, in which James played, resulted in a 1–0 defeat at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NorthEast_United" title="NorthEast United">NorthEast United</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> His team eventually became the runners up in the inaugural ISL tournament by losing to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atletico_de_Kolkata" title="Atletico de Kolkata">Atletico de Kolkata</a> 1-0 in the finals.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DaJa.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="503" height="306" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/DaJa.JPG/220px-DaJa.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/DaJa.JPG/330px-DaJa.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/DaJa.JPG/440px-DaJa.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DaJa.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
James in <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> colours, 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After making one <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">England under-21</a> appearance whilst at Watford, James made his full debut for <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Hoddle" title="Glenn Hoddle">Glenn Hoddle</a>'s England in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Friendly_match" title="Friendly match">friendly</a> against <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> on 29 March 1997 when he was a Liverpool player. He kept his first international clean sheet as England beat Mexico 2–0 with goals from <a href="/wiki/Teddy_Sheringham" title="Teddy Sheringham">Teddy Sheringham</a> and James' Liverpool team mate <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a>. He was in the provisional 28-man squad for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_2000" title="Euro 2000">Euro 2000</a> before missing the final cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>James is the only black goalkeeper to represent England as a full international.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>For several years he had to play understudy to England's regular keeper, <a href="/wiki/David_Seaman" title="David Seaman">David Seaman</a>. When Seaman was dropped after making a mistake against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia_national_football_team" title="Republic of Macedonia national football team">FYR Macedonia</a> in 2002, James became the new England number one. He retained his place in the England team even after West Ham's relegation to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a> in 2003, and was the only player from outside the top flight to win an England cap between 1999 (<a href="/wiki/Michael_Gray_(footballer)" title="Michael Gray (footballer)">Michael Gray</a>) and 2007 (<a href="/wiki/David_Nugent" title="David Nugent">David Nugent</a>). He went on to play in all of England's matches at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_UEFA_European_Football_Championship" title="2004 UEFA European Football Championship">Euro 2004</a>.</p>
<p>James was dropped from the starting XI after an error in a 2–2 <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> qualifying draw against <a href="/wiki/Austria_national_football_team" title="Austria national football team">Austria</a> in September 2004, his place being taken by Tottenham's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_Robinson_(goalkeeper)" title="Paul Robinson (goalkeeper)">Paul Robinson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>James came on as a half-time substitute and conceded all four goals in the 4–1 drubbing England suffered at the hands of <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a> during a friendly on 17 August 2005 – their worst defeat in 25 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> James still remained part of the England squad, and was selected as the second-choice goalkeeper behind Robinson for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a> in Germany, though he did not play.</p>
<p>Along with fellow veterans <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sol_Campbell" title="Sol Campbell">Sol Campbell</a>, James was dropped from the England squad at the start of <a href="/wiki/Steve_McClaren" title="Steve McClaren">Steve McClaren</a>'s reign and was not called up during the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_in_English_football" title="2006–07 in English football">2006–07 season</a>. He was recalled for the friendly with <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> on 22 August 2007, over a year since first being omitted. James played the whole of the second half of England's 2–1 defeat to Germany as a substitute for Robinson. In so doing, he became the first Portsmouth player to play for the senior England team since <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hateley" title="Mark Hateley">Mark Hateley</a> in 1984. However, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Carson" title="Scott Carson">Scott Carson</a> was chosen ahead of both James and Robinson for the decisive Euro 2008 qualifier against Croatia on 21 November 2007. England lost the match and Carson was blamed for Croatia's opening goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Following England's failure to qualify for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">Euro 2008</a> McClaren was sacked as England manager and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Fabio_Capello" title="Fabio Capello">Fabio Capello</a>. James was subsequently critical of McClaren's treatment of England's goalkeepers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 February 2008, James was selected as goalkeeper for Capello's first match in charge, a friendly against <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a>. It was his first start for England since a friendly with <a href="/wiki/Colombia_national_football_team" title="Colombia national football team">Colombia</a> in May 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> James firmly re-established himself as England's first choice goalkeeper, starting in each of Capello's first 13 games in charge. Persistent injury problems over the following year left James' hopes of retaining the No. 1 spot for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_World_Cup" title="2010 World Cup">2010 World Cup</a> in doubt, with Capello stating he would only consider players who were 100% fit for his squad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">World Cup qualifier</a> against <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_national_football_team" title="Ukraine national football team">Ukraine</a> on 1 April 2009, James did not start a match for England until the final friendly before the World Cup against <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a> on 30 May 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_World_Cup">2010 World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2010 World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Prior to the tournament, James was backed to reclaim the number one shirt by former England goalkeepers <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Banks" title="Gordon Banks">Gordon Banks</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/David_Seaman" title="David Seaman">David Seaman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 June 2010, it was confirmed that James would be travelling to the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">World Cup Finals</a> in South Africa, and would be allocated the number 1 jersey. He was the oldest footballer in the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> James was not selected for the first game of the World Cup against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">United States</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Robert_Green" title="Robert Green">Robert Green</a> instead starting in the England goal. However, Green made an error that allowed <a href="/wiki/Clint_Dempsey" title="Clint Dempsey">Clint Dempsey</a> to score an equaliser that resulted in the game being drawn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> James returned to the starting line-up in the next game, keeping a clean sheet against <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a> on 18 June 2010. In doing so James became the oldest ever World Cup debutant at 39 years and 321 days old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Five days later, he kept another clean sheet as England won against <a href="/wiki/Slovenia_national_football_team" title="Slovenia national football team">Slovenia</a> 1–0 to ensure that they would reach the last 16, although they finished second in Group C behind the United States. They were eliminated in the following round after a 4–1 defeat to Germany.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coaching_career">Coaching career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Coaching career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Luton_Town">Luton Town</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Luton Town">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following a player-coach role at Icelandic side IBV earlier in the year October 2013 saw James join <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a> in a coaching capacity in order to gain experience towards a <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> A-licence qualification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kerala_Blasters_FC_2">Kerala Blasters FC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Kerala Blasters FC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>He was the player-manager of <a href="/wiki/Kerala_Blasters_FC" title="Kerala Blasters FC">Kerala Blasters FC</a> in <a href="/wiki/Indian_Super_League" title="Indian Super League">Indian Super League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KB_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-KB-54">[54]</a></sup> He helped the blasters win the runners up title of Indian super league.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_Jamesgoalkeeper2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="692" data-file-width="494" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/David_Jamesgoalkeeper2.jpg/150px-David_Jamesgoalkeeper2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/David_Jamesgoalkeeper2.jpg/225px-David_Jamesgoalkeeper2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/David_Jamesgoalkeeper2.jpg/300px-David_Jamesgoalkeeper2.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:David_Jamesgoalkeeper2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
James in 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>James was brought up in <a href="/wiki/Welwyn_Garden_City" title="Welwyn Garden City">Welwyn Garden City</a>, attending the Sir Frederic Osborn School.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> He has four children with his former wife Tanya,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> whom he divorced in 2005, and presently lives in <a href="/wiki/Chudleigh" title="Chudleigh">Chudleigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a> with his current partner, Amanda Salmon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>James has gained attention for modelling assignments, first with <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Armani" title="Giorgio Armani">Giorgio Armani</a> in 1995,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> and with <a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a> in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>James was known for experimenting with his hairstyle. In May 2007, a "Who Ate All the Pies" column ridiculed him, among David Beckham and others,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> for "backcombed efforts",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> and likened a previous November 2006 cut to fictional character <a href="/wiki/Clark_Kent" title="Clark Kent">Clark Kent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> both captured by BBC <i><a href="/wiki/Match_of_the_Day" title="Match of the Day">Match of the Day</a></i>.</p>
<p>During the 2003 off-season, James was a guest at the training camp of <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> team the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a>, where he studied their training and conditioning methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_work">Charity work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Charity work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2005, James visited the south eastern African nation of <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a> to help raise <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">AIDS</a> awareness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> He subsequently set up the David James Foundation in order to help <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a> farmers in Malawi develop more efficient production techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The foundation also aims to give teenagers the skills, such as mechanical and construction skills, needed to go out and work. James has also made connections with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Exe_Technology_College" title="West Exe Technology College">West Exe Technology College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a>. This college has brought to his attention the Malawian charity, Friends of Mulanje Orphans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The foundation funds the David James Foundation Scholarship at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Westminster" title="University of Westminster">University of Westminster</a>, which funds a student from Malawi to study for a <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master's degree</a> at Westminster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The charity has been supported by the <a href="/wiki/Institution_of_Chemical_Engineers" title="Institution of Chemical Engineers">Institution of Chemical Engineers</a> (IChemE).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chem_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-chem-89">[89]</a></sup> James is also a global ambassador for the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a> and works with Access Sport to provide sports provision in deprived areas of the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing">Writing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Writing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition to being an art lover, James writes a regular column for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> newspaper, and donates his article fee to charity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> James was also the illustrator on the children's book <i>Harry's Magic Pockets: The Circus</i> written by his friend, Steve Pearson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bankruptcy">Bankruptcy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Bankruptcy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2014 James was declared <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">bankrupt</a>. Despite earning an estimated £20m from his footballing career, owning several properties and having a lucrative contract modeling for Armani, James' debts had built up since his divorce from his wife, Tanya, in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2014, James placed for sale hundreds of items of football <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorabilia" title="Memorabilia">memorabilia</a> collected during his career, to pay off the debts. Items included 150 signed shirts, shorts and match balls as well as his customised <a href="/wiki/Vauxhall_Astra" title="Vauxhall Astra">Vauxhall Astra</a> van and <a href="/wiki/Raleigh_Chopper" title="Raleigh Chopper">Raleigh Chopper</a> bikes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_career">Media career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_James_(footballer,_born_1970)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Media career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Shortly before <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a>, James presented a <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> programme entitled <i>Euro's Most Shocking Moments</i> alongside <a href="/wiki/Richard_Bacon_(broadcaster)" title="Richard Bacon (broadcaster)">Richard Bacon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the summer of 2013, it was announced that James would become a TV pundit for <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a>'s coverage of <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conference_Premier" title="Conference Premier">Conference Premier</a> matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> He usually appears beside <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Currie" title="Darrell Currie">Darrell Currie</a> on the touchline at some matches alongside other guests.</p>
<p>James worked as a pundit for <a href="/wiki/Eurosport" title="Eurosport">Eurosport</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>.</p>
